The Contribution of al-Ahmadi Abadi to Hanafi Scholarship
Biography of a Hanafi commentator and his works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of Sheikh Noor al-Din al-Ahmadi Abadi and explain the role of hawashi in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Hawashi are not mere glosses; they preserve the living tradition of Hanafi legal analysis across generations.

This lesson introduces you to a prolific Hanafi commentator who wrote supercommentaries on foundational texts of fiqh, usul, tafsir, and logic. Understanding his works helps you appreciate the depth and continuity of the Hanafi madhhab, especially the tradition of refinement through hawashi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar and His Lineage
Read the passage carefully to extract the full name of the scholar and notice the title 'Sheikh'. Note that his father is also named, indicating a scholarly lineage.
Full name: Sheikh Noor al-Din ibn Sheikh Muhammad Salih al-Ahmadi Abadi.
2
List His Commented Works
Identify each text mentioned as a work he wrote supercommentaries on. Pay attention to the range of disciplines represented.
Works include Sharh al-Wiqaya (fiqh), al-Talwih (usul al-fiqh), Tafsir al-Baydawi (tafsir), Sharh al-Mawaqif (kalam), etc.
3
Determine His Lifespan
Locate the birth and death dates given in the passage. Convert to Common Era if needed to situate him historically.
Birth: 1064 AH (≈1654 CE); Death: 1155 AH (≈1742 CE). He lived in the 11th-12th centuries AH, a period of rich Hanafi scholarship in India.
4
Understand the Significance of Hawashi
Reflect on why a scholar would write hawashi on so many major works. Consider that hawashi are not mere summaries but often contain original analysis, resolutions of debates, and refinements of the madhhab.
Writing hawashi was a standard method of scholarly contribution and teaching in the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٦. ومنهم: الشيخ نور الدين ابن الشيخ محمد صالح الأحمد آبادي، صاحب التصانيف الكثيرة ، منها : حواش كل من «شرح الوقاية»، و«التلويح»، و«العضدي»، و«المطول»، و«تفسير البيضاوي»، و«شرح المواقف»، و«القديمة»، و«شرح المقاصد»، و «شرح المطالع»، و«الفوائد الضيائية»، وغير ذلك، كانت ولادته سنة أربع وستين وألف»، ووفاته سنة خمس وخمسين بعد الألف والمئة. كذا في «سبحة المرجان».
46. Among them: Sheikh Noor al-Din ibn Sheikh Muhammad Salih al-Ahmadi Abadi, author of numerous works, among them: supercommentaries on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', 'al-Talwih', 'al-Adudi', 'al-Mutawwal', 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'Sharh al-Mawaqif', 'al-Qadima', 'Sharh al-Maqasid', 'Sharh al-Matali', 'al-Fawa'id al-Diya'iyya', and others. His birth was in the year 1064 AH, and his death in 1155 AH. Thus in 'Sabhat al-Marjan'.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from Umdat al-Ri'aya, listing the scholars who wrote supercommentaries (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqaya. Sheikh Noor al-Din is introduced as a prolific author, having written hawashi on many major works across fiqh, usul, tafsir, and logic. His birth and death dates place him in the 11th-12th centuries AH. This shows the depth of the Hanafi scholarly tradition in India.

Key Terms
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqaya): A famous Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Sadr al-Shari'a al-Mahbubi, commonly studied in the curriculum.
حواش (hawashi): Supercommentaries (plural of hashia) that comment on a primary commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1064 AH
B) 1155 AH
C) 1164 AH
D) 1065 AH

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Noor al-Din al-Ahmadi Abadi exemplified the Hanafi tradition of scholarly refinement through supercommentaries across multiple disciplines.

The Life and Legacy of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf
Detailed biography of a Hanafi mufti and teacher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly lineage, education, and contributions of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, and explain how his biography reflects the Hanafi tradition in India.

Core Idea
A mufti's lineage and works reveal the living chain of Hanafi transmission from the Companions to 19th-century India.

Mufti Muhammad Yusuf was a towering Hanafi scholar from the famous Firangi Mahal family in Lucknow. This biography, written by a later scholar, traces his ancestry back to the Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and details his education, teaching, and fatwa work. It also lists his unfinished scholarly works, showing the breadth of his learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his lineage
Read the beginning of the passage to find the full name and death date of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf. Then, trace the chain of ancestors mentioned, noting the final link to the Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari.
The lineage shows connection to the Prophet's Companion, a source of spiritual and scholarly authority.
2
Map his education
Identify all teachers named in the text and the subjects or books studied under each. List them in order.
Teachers include his father, Mufti Zuhur Allah, and his brother.
3
Trace his career
Note the positions he held: mufti of his town, then teacher at Janpur. Identify the years and events that triggered these changes, such as his father's death and the Indian revolt.
The text mentions the 'fitna' (revolt) of 1272 AH (1857).
4
Identify his works
List all the works attributed to Mufti Muhammad Yusuf. Pay attention to which are incomplete.
Many are supercommentaries (hawashi) on standard texts.
5
Evaluate his legacy
Based on the descriptions in the text, summarize the qualities for which he was praised. Consider his learning, spirituality, and the fact that he died in Medina and was buried in al-Baqi.
His death in Medina is seen as a blessed end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٧. ومنهم : أستاذ أستاذي عم والدي، مولانا المفتي محمد يوسف بن المفتي محمد أصغر، المتوفى في التاسع عشر من رجب سنة خمس وخمسين بعد الألف والمئتين، يوم السبت، ابن المفتي أبي الرحم بن ملا محمد يعقوب بن مولانا عبد العزيز – المتوفّى لتسع خلون من ذي العقدة سنة ست وستين ، وقيل : سنة خمس وستين بعد الألف والمئة - ابن ملا سعيد بن ملاً قطب الدين الشهيد السهالوي – المتوفى في يوم الاثنين التاسع عشر من رجب سنة إحدى وقيل : ثلاث بعد الألف والمئة – ابن الشيخ عبد الحليم بن الشيخ عبد الكريم بن الشيخ أحمد بن الشيخ حافظ ، وهو من أحفاد الشيخ علاء الدين الأنصاري، وهو من أحفاد خواجه عبد الله الأنصاري، من نسل سيدنا أبي أيوب الأنصاري الصحابي . وليطلب تمام نسبه وتراجم ،آبائه، وكذا تراجم كثير من أعزّتي وأقاربي وعلماء بلدة لكنو المقيمين في محلة فرنجى محلّ، من رسالتي : (خير العمل في تراجم أهل فرنجى محل» التي جعلتها جزءاً لرسالتي «إنباء الخلان بأنباء علماء هندوستان». كان رحمه الله يوسف عصره في الجمال والكمال، جامعاً للفروع والأصول، حاوياً للمعقول والمنقول ، ذا مجاهدة ورياضة، وعبادة ومكاشفة، متهجداً متعبداً، ولد في حياة جده سنة ثلاث وعشرين بعد الألف ،والمئتين، وقرأ أكثر الكتب الدرسية بحضرة والده، وقدراً منها بحضرة مولانا المفتي ظهور الله ، و«الرسالة القوشجيّة» بحضرة أخيه مولانا نور الله المرحوم. سنة. وبايع على يد مولانا أحمد أنوار الحق المتوفّى في السادس والعشرين من شعبان - ست وثلاثين بعد الألف والمئتين - ابن مولانا أحمد عبد الحق – المتوفى في يوم الجمعة تاسع ذي الحجة من السنة السابعة والستين بعد الألف والمئة – ابن ملا سعيد بن القطب الشهيد. وتعلّم أكثر الأذكار والأوراد من مولانا عبد الوالي – المتوفّى في شعبان سنة تسع وسبعين بعد الألف والمئتين - ابن مولانا أبي الكرم بن مولانا يعقوب المقدّم . ذكره. ولما توفي والده المفتي محمد أصغر ، فُوِّض إليه إفتاء العدالة ببلدتنا فقام به بحسن الديانة إلى زمان فتنة الهند، وانتزاع السلطة، وهو سنة اثنتين وسبعين ، ثم صار مدرساً بجونفور بمدرسة الحاج إمام بخش المرحوم حين سافر والدي المرحوم إلى حيدر آباد الدكن، وكان مدرساً بها، وذلك سنة سبع وسبعين ، فدرس هناك إلى سنة ســت وثمانين، واستفاد منه خلق كثير. وسافر في شعبان من السنة المذكورة من جونفور إلى الحرمين الشريفين، ودخل مكة المعظمة في آخر رمضان، وارتحل في آخرِ شوال إلى المدينة الطيبة، وابتلي من أثناء الطريق بالحمى والإسهال الكبدي، فتوفى بالمدينة، ودفن بالبقيع فطوبى له من حسن خاتمة وفضل مضجع ومدفن، وكان ذلك. يوم الأحد تاسع عشر ذي القعدة سنة ست وثمانين. وله تأليفات شاهدة على مهارته وتبحره، منها: «حواشي شرح السلّم» لملا حسن بن القاضي غلام مصطفى بن ملاً أسعد بن القطب الشهيد ، ومنها : حواشي شرح السلم للقاضي مبارك ، ومنها : حواشي الشمس البازغة»، ومنها : تكملة حواشي الشمس البازغة» لملا حسن، ومنها : حواش على طبيعيات الشفاء» للشيخ أبي علي ابن سينا، ولم تتم ومنها : حواشي شرح الوقاية من الابتداء إلى بحث مسح الرأس ولم تتم، وله تعليقات متشتته على تفسير البيضاوي»، و«صحيح البخاري»، وغير ذلك.
47. Among them: the teacher of my teacher, my father's uncle, our master the Mufti Muhammad Yusuf ibn Mufti Muhammad Asghar, who died on the 19th of Rajab in the year 1255 AH, on Saturday, son of Mufti Abu al-Rahm ibn Mulla Muhammad Ya'qub ibn Mawlana Abd al-Aziz – who died on the 9th of Dhu al-Qa'dah in the year 66, reportedly 65 AH – ibn Mulla Sa'id ibn Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Shahid al-Sahalawi – who died on Monday 19th of Rajab in the year 1 or 3 AH – ibn Sheikh Abd al-Halim ibn Sheikh Abd al-Karim ibn Sheikh Ahmad ibn Sheikh Hafiz, and he is among the descendants of Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Ansari, and of Khwaja Abd Allah al-Ansari, from the lineage of our master Abu Ayyub al-Ansari the Companion. Let the full lineage and biographies of his ancestors, as well as biographies of many of my dear ones, relatives, and scholars of the city of Lucknow residing in Firangi Mahal, be sought from my treatise (Khayr al-'Amal fi Tarajim Ahl Firangi Mahal) which I made as a part of my treatise Inba' al-Khillan bi-Anba' 'Ulama' Hindustan. He was, may Allah have mercy on him, the Joseph of his time in beauty and perfection, combining jurisprudence and principles, encompassing rational and transmitted knowledge, possessing struggle and spiritual exercise, worship and unveiling, a night-prayerful worshiper. He was born during the lifetime of his grandfather in the year 23 AH, and read most of the advanced books under his father, and some under our master Mufti Zuhur Allah, and al-Risala al-Qushjiyya under his brother Mawlana Nur Allah. He gave allegiance to Mawlana Ahmad Anwar al-Haqq – who died on 26th Sha'ban 1236 AH – son of Mawlana Ahmad Abd al-Haqq – who died on Friday 9th Dhu al-Hijjah 67 AH – son of Mulla Sa'id ibn al-Qutb al-Shahid. He learned most litanies and daily recitations from Mawlana Abd al-Wali – who died in Sha'ban 1279 AH – son of Mawlana Abi al-Karam ibn Mawlana Ya'qub al-Muqaddam. When his father Mufti Muhammad Asghar died, the position of issuing fatwas for justice in our town was entrusted to him, and he upheld it with good devotion until the time of the Indian revolt and the seizure of power, which was the year 72, then he became a teacher in Janpur at the school of Hajji Imam Bakhsh when my father traveled to Hyderabad Deccan, and he was a teacher there, in the year 77, and taught there until the year 86, and many people benefited from him. He traveled in Sha'ban of the mentioned year from Janpur to the Two Holy Sanctuaries, entered Mecca at the end of Ramadan, and left at the end of Shawwal to Medina, and was afflicted on the way with fever and hepatic diarrhea, and died in Medina, and was buried in al-Baqi. Blessed be his good end and excellent resting place. That was on Sunday 19th Dhu al-Qa'dah in the year 86. He has works testifying to his skill and deep knowledge, including: 'Hawashi Sharh al-Sullam' by Mulla Hasan ibn al-Qadi Ghulam Mustafa ibn Mulla As'ad ibn al-Qutb al-Shahid, and 'Hawashi Sharh al-Sullam' by al-Qadi Mubarak, and 'Hawashi al-Shams al-Bazigha', and 'Takmila Hawashi al-Shams al-Bazigha' by Mulla Hasan, and 'Hawashi 'ala Tabi'iyyat al-Shifa'' by Sheikh Abi Ali ibn Sina (unfinished), and 'Hawashi Sharh al-Wiqaya' from the beginning to the section on wiping the head (unfinished), and scattered annotations on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi' and 'Sahih al-Bukhari' and others.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is a detailed biography of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, a prominent Hanafi scholar from Lucknow. The author describes his lineage tracing back to the companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, his education under his father and others, his appointment as mufti, his teaching at Janpur, his travel to Mecca and Medina, and his death in Medina. His works include incomplete supercommentaries on several texts. This biography highlights the scholarly network and the academic tradition in 18th-19th century India.

Key Terms
مفتي (mufti): A scholar authorized to issue fatwas (legal opinions) in the Hanafi madhhab.
إفتاء (ifta'): The act of issuing fatwas; the office or function of a mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Janpur
C) Medina
D) Mecca

Key Takeaway
Mufti Muhammad Yusuf's biography exemplifies the transmission of Hanafi knowledge through lineage, teachers, and scholarly works in India.

Biography of Sheikh Abdul Halim (Author's Father)
Biographical note on the author's father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Sheikh Abdul Halim and explain his role in the author's scholarly formation.

Core Idea
The author's father was both his teacher and his intellectual anchor.

This passage introduces the author's father, Sheikh Abdul Halim, a Hafiz and scholar who taught his son Arabic morphology and grammar. The biographical note situates the author within a lineage of Hanafi learning. Understanding this chain helps appreciate the isnad (chain) of knowledge transmission in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and his titles
Look for names, honorifics like 'Mawlana', 'Hafiz', 'Hajj'. Note the full name: Abdul Halim ibn Amin Allah.
Hafiz indicates memorization of the Qur'an; Hajj indicates pilgrimage.
2
Locate key dates
Find the death year (1253 AH) and birth date (21 Sha'ban, year 39).
Birth year is likely 1239 AH based on context.
3
Identify scholarly activities
He memorized the Qur'an and read books of morphology (sarf) and grammar (nahw).
These are foundational sciences for fiqh.
4
Note the family connection
He is the author's father, and the author credits him for his knowledge.
The author mentions his grandfather and great-grandfather as part of the scholarly lineage.

Source Text

ومنهم : والدي ومن إليه في العلوم استنادي ، مولانا الحافظ الحاج عبد الحليم بن مولانا أمين الله - المتوفى سنة ثلاث وخمسين بعد الألف والمئتين – ابن مولانا محمد أكبر بـن المفتي أبي ) الرحم المقدّم ذكره، ولد في الحادي والعشرين من شعبان سنة تسع وثلاثين، وحفظ القرآن وقرأ كتب الصرف والنحو على والده.
Among them: my father, to whom I attribute my knowledge, our master al-Hafiz al-Hajj Abdul Halim ibn Mawlana Amin Allah – died in the year 1253 AH – ibn Mawlana Muhammad Akbar ibn al-Mufti Abu al-Rahm (previously mentioned), born on the 21st of Sha'ban in the year 39 (1239 AH?), memorized the Qur'an and read books of morphology and grammar on his father.

Commentary
This short biography introduces the author's father, Sheikh Abdul Halim, as a scholar who memorized the Qur'an and studied Arabic grammar under his own father. The date of death is given as 1253 AH. This personal note shows the chain of learning within the family.

Key Terms
حافظ (hafiz): One who has memorized the entire Qur'an, often a title of respect.
الصرف والنحو (al-sarf wa al-nahw): Morphology and grammar (of Arabic); foundational sciences for understanding Quran and Hadith.

The Scholarly Journey of a Hanafi Scholar: Study, Travel, and Ijaza
Biographical account of a scholar's education, teachers, travels, and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the key stages of a Hanafi scholar's education and explain the role of ijaza and travel in establishing scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar gains authority through a chain of teachers, extensive travel, and multiple ijazat.

This passage narrates the biography of a prominent Hanafi scholar from India, detailing his education under various teachers, his travels to teach and obtain ijazat, and his final position as a judge. Understanding this journey illuminates the traditional path of acquiring and transmitting sacred knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's teachers and subjects studied
List the teachers mentioned and the books/subjects studied with each: e.g., Mufti Zahur Allah (Sharh Talkhis al-Miftah), Mufti Muhammad Asghar (Sharh al-Wiqayah, Nur al-Anwar, etc.), and others.
This establishes the scholarly lineage and curriculum of the Hanafi madrasa.
2
Trace the scholar's travels and teaching appointments
Note the cities (Bandeh, Jaunpur, Hyderabad, Mecca/Medina) and the teaching positions he held at each. These travels show the interconnected scholarly network.
Travel (rihla) is a key component of seeking knowledge and spreading it.
3
Determine the importance of ijaza
The scholar received many ijazat from scholars in the Hijaz, including the Hanafi mufti of Mecca. Ijaza is a certification of competence to transmit knowledge.
Ijaza authenticates the chain of transmission and grants authority.
4
Note the scholarly network
The scholar connected Indian Hanafis with Hijazi scholars, indicating a transregional scholarly community.
This network ensured the preservation and propagation of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Recognize the culmination: judgeship and death
He was appointed to manage supreme judicial justice (nazamat al-adala) in Hyderabad and died in 1285 AH. His career shows the integration of scholarship and legal practice.
Judgeship represents the highest trust in applying fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد وفاته قرأ نبذا من «شرح تلخيص المفتاح» على جد أبيه الفاسد مولانا المفتي ظهور الله بن ملا محمد ولي صاحب التصانيف الشهيرة : كالحواشي على «الحواش الزاهدية الثلاثة المشهورة المتعلّقة بحاشية «التهذيب الجلالية» والمتعلقة بـ«الرسالة القطبية»، والمتعلقة بـ «شرح المواقف»، وغير ذلك ، المتوفى في السنة السادسة والخمسين. العقائد وقرأ نبذاً من الكتب الدرسية كـ«شرح الوقاية»، و«نور الأنوار»، و«شرح النسفية»، وغيرها على المفتي محمّد أصغر عمّ والده، وبعد وفاتـه قـرأ بقية الكتب الدرسية معقولاً ومنقولاً على المفتي محمد يوسف المقدم ذكره، وقرأ كتب العلـم الرياضي على خاله مولانا محمد نعمت الله - المتوفى ببلدة بنارس في المحرم سنة تسعين – ابن مولانا نور الله بن ملا محمّد ولي بن القاضي غلام مصطفى بن ملا سعد القطب الشهيد. وبرع في جميع العلوم العقلية والنقلية، وفاز بمرتبة التحقيق في جميع الفنون الفرعية والأصلية، وسافر من وطنه إلى بلدة بانـده سنة ستين ، فجعله النواب ذو الفقار الدولة المرحوم مدرساً بمدرسته، فأقام هناك يدرس ويفيد ، ثم سافر إلى جونفور، فجعله الحاج محمد إمام بخش رئيس تلك البلدة - المتوفى بمكة المعظمة سنة ثمان وسبعين – مدرّساً بمدرسته، وقد تلمذ عليه خلق كثير حين إقامته بهاتين المدرستين، واشتهرت فضائله وفتاواه وتصانيفه بين الخافقين، حتى فُضْلَ على أساتذته وفضلاء عصره. ثم سافر إلى بلدة حيدر آباد الدكن سنة ، سبع وسبعين ، فجعله وزير السلطنة الآصفية النوّاب مختار الملك بهادر دام إقباله مدرسا بمدرسته ، فأقام فيها يدرس ويفيد ، ثم استعفى عنه لعوائق عرضت له، وسافر إلى الحرمين الشريفين ، سنة تسع وسبعين ، فأكرمه علماؤهما وأجازوه : منهم : مفتي الحنفية بمكة مولانا محمد جمال)، المتوفى سنة أربع وثمانين. ومفتي الشافعية بها : مولانا السيد أحمد دحلان. وشيخ الدلائل : الشيخ علي الحريري المدني) المرحوم. ومولانا عبد الغني المجددي الدهلوي)، المتوفى سنة ست وتسعين. ومولانا عبد الرشيد المجددي، وغيرهم. وكانت له إجازة سابقة من مولانا حسين أحمد المحدث المليح آبادي)، تلميذ الشيخ مولانا عبد العزيز الدهلوي. ثم رجع إلى حيدر آباد سنة ثمانين في ربيع الآخر، ففوض إليه الوزير الممدوح نظامة العدالة العالية الديوانية، فتوجه إلى فصل الخصومات بحسن النظام إلى أن توفي هناك يوم الإثنين التاسع والعشرين من شعبان من سنة خمس وثمانين، وله تصانيف
After his death he read selections from 'Sharh Talkhis al-Miftah' under his father's uncle, the venerable Mufti Zahur Allah ibn Mulla Muhammad Wali, author of famous works such as glosses on the three well-known 'Zawāhidī Glosses' related to the gloss of 'al-Tahdhīb al-Jalāliyyah', related to 'al-Risālah al-Qutbiyyah', and related to 'Sharh al-Mawāqif', and others, who died in the year fifty-six. [He read] beliefs and read selections from the standard books like 'Sharh al-Wiqāyah', 'Nūr al-Anwār', 'Sharh al-Nasafiyyah' and others under Mufti Muhammad Asghar, his father's uncle. After his death he read the rest of the standard books, rational and transmitted, under Mufti Muhammad Yusuf mentioned previously. And he read books of mathematical science under his maternal uncle Maulānā Muhammad Ni'mat Allah - who died in the town of Banaras in Muharram of the year ninety – son of Maulānā Nūr Allāh ibn Mulla Muhammad Wali ibn al-Qādi Ghulām Mustafā ibn Mulla Sa'd al-Qutb al-Shahīd. He excelled in all rational and transmitted sciences, and attained the rank of verification (tahqīq) in all subsidiary and fundamental disciplines. He travelled from his homeland to the town of Bandeh in the year sixty, and Nawāb Dhu al-Faqār al-Dawla, the deceased, made him a teacher in his school. He settled there teaching and benefitting. Then he travelled to Jaunpur, and Hājj Muhammad Imām Bakhsh, the chief of that town - who died in Mecca in the year seventy-eight – made him a teacher in his school. A great many students studied under him during his stay in these two schools. His virtues, fatwas, and works became famous between the two horizons, such that he was preferred over his teachers and the eminent men of his time. Then he travelled to the city of Hyderabad Deccan in the year seventy-seven. The minister of the Asafiyyah kingdom, Nawāb Mukhtār al-Mulk Bahādur Dām Iqbalah, made him a teacher in his school. He settled there teaching and benefitting. Then he resigned due to obstacles that arose for him, and travelled to the two noble sanctuaries (Mecca and Medina) in the year seventy-nine. Their scholars honoured him and gave him ijāzah: among them the Mufti of the Hanafis in Mecca, Maulānā Muhammad Jamāl, who died in the year eighty-four, and the Mufti of the Shāfi'īs there, Maulānā al-Sayyid Ahmad Dahlān, and Shaykh al-Dalā'il: al-Shaykh 'Alī al-Harīrī al-Madanī, the deceased, and Maulānā 'Abd al-Ghanī al-Mujaddidī al-Dihlawī, who died in the year ninety-six, and Maulānā 'Abd al-Rashīd al-Mujaddidī, and others. He had received a prior ijāzah from Maulānā Husayn Ahmad al-Muhaddith al-Malīh Abādī, student of Shaykh Maulānā 'Abd al-'Azīz al-Dihlawī. Then he returned to Hyderabad in Rabī' al-Akhīr of the year eighty. The praised minister entrusted him with the management of the supreme judicial (Dīwānī) justice. He turned to settling disputes with excellent system until he died there on Monday the 29th of Sha'bān of the year eighty-five. He has works [including...]
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account (tarjamah) of a Hanafi scholar, detailing his academic lineage, teachers, travels, and appointments. The text begins by mentioning his studies after the death of a relative under Mufti Zahur Allah, who was a prolific author of glosses (hawāshī). He then studied standard texts of the Hanafi madrasa curriculum, such as 'Sharh al-Wiqāyah' (a foundational Hanafi fiqh text), 'Nūr al-Anwār' (a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work), and 'Sharh al-Nasafiyyah' (a work on creed). His teachers include Mufti Muhammad Asghar and Mufti Muhammad Yusuf. He also studied mathematics (al-‘ilm al-riyādī) under his maternal uncle. The phrase 'baraza fī jamī‘ al-‘ulūm al-‘aqliyyah wa al-naqliyyah' indicates he mastered both rational sciences (philosophy, logic) and transmitted sciences (Qur'an, Hadith, fiqh). He achieved the rank of 'tahqīq' (verification/investigation). He travelled extensively for teaching: first to Bandeh (possibly Banda), then Jaunpur, then Hyderabad Deccan. He also performed Hajj and visited Mecca and Medina, where he received multiple ijāzāt from prominent scholars, including the Hanafi mufti of Mecca and the Shāfi‘ī mufti. His return to Hyderabad saw him appointed as a judge (nazāmat al-‘adālat al-‘āliyyah al-dīwāniyyah). He died in 1285 AH (on a Monday). This biography underscores the importance of scholarly travel (riḥlah fī ṭalab al-‘ilm), obtaining ijāzah, and the interconnectedness of the scholarly network across India and the Hijaz in the 13th century AH.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijāzah): A formal permission or license from a scholar to transmit a book or teach a subject, often given after verifying the student's competence.
التدريس (al-tadrīs): Teaching; the scholar was appointed as mudarris (teacher) in various madrasas.
مفتي الحنفية (muftī al-ḥanafiyyah): The chief Hanafi jurisconsult in Mecca, a recognized authority for issuing fatwas according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which scholar gave the subject of this biography an early ijāzah?
A) Mufti Muhammad Jamal
B) Maulana Husayn Ahmad al-Malih Abadi

D) Mufti Muhammad Asghar

Key Takeaway
This biography illustrates that a Hanafi scholar's authority is built through a diverse education, travel for ijāzāt, and service as teacher and judge.

Life of the Author

Reading Tarajim: Hanafi Commentators on Sharh al-Wiqaya
Biographical list of Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a Hanafi biographical notice (tarjama) and trace the scholarly lineage of a commentator on Sharh al-Wiqaya.

Core Idea
Hanafi tarajim establish authority by linking each scholar to teachers, works, and death dates.

This passage presents the biographies (tarajim) of several Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries or annotations on Sharh al-Wiqaya, a key text in the school. Understanding these biographical notices is essential for evaluating the reliability and chain of transmission of the commentaries we use. The author meticulously records names, lineages, teachers, and works, often noting scholarly interactions such as plagiarism or chains of initiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Look for the complete name starting with 'ibn' or 'bin', tracing back to notable figures like al-Qutb al-Shahid. This establishes the scholarly pedigree.
Lineage often includes multiple generations, e.g., 'ibn Mulla Muhibb Allah ibn Ahmad...'
2
Note the death date and place
Death dates are given in Hijri years and sometimes locations (e.g., Hyderabad Deccan). This helps contextualize the scholar's era.
The author uses phrases like 'al-mutawaffa fi...' to indicate death.
3
List the teachers and students
Teachers are mentioned explicitly (e.g., 'akhadha al-ilm an kumala dahr') and sometimes by naming their own teachers. Students can be inferred from chains of transmission.
Pay attention to phrases like 'talmidh' or 'qara' a'la'.
4
Extract the works authored
The passage lists several titles; note which are commentaries on Sharh al-Wiqaya and which are independent treatises. The author sometimes critiques the originality of works.
Look for 'lahu' followed by the work title.

The eighth study: Biographies of the commentators on Sharh al-Wiqaya. 133 ... and seventy after one thousand and two hundred - son of our master Muhammad Haydar - died in Hyderabad Deccan in Muharram of the year fifty-six - son of the author of famous works such as Sharh al-Sullam and others, our master Muhammad Mubin - died in Rabi' al-Akhir of the year twenty-five - son of Mulla Muhibb Allah ibn our master Ahmad Abd al-Haqq ibn Mulla Sa'id ibn al-Qutb al-Shahid, previously mentioned. He has: two treatises in Arabic and Persian related to the discussion of the Indian circle occurring in Sharh al-Wiqaya, and he also has scattered annotations on Sharh al-Wiqaya, and he has a treatise related to the discussion of al-Hasil wa al-Mahsul from al-Fawa'id al-Diya'iyya. 50. Among them: al-Mawlawi al-Sayyid Abu al-Khayr Muhammad Mu'in al-Din al-Karwi - attributed to Kara, with fatha on the kaf and the Persian ray: a town known near Ilahabad - son of Shah Khayrat Ali ibn al-Sayyid Ahmad ibn Shah Qiyam al-Din, and his lineage ends with Imam Musa al-Kazim. He has: a commentary related to the discussion of the intervening purity, naming it al-Ta'liq al-Kamil, and my father the scholar followed him in places in Muntahiyat al-Ta'liq al-Fasil. Among his works: a treatise on the discussion of al-Muthanna bi al-Takrar, Marqat al-Adhhan fi 'Ilm al-Mizan, Mir'at al-Adhhan fi 'Ilm al-Wajib, al-Adab al-Mu'ayyana fi al-Munazara, Jala' al-Adhhan fi 'Ilm al-Qur'an, Hidayat al-Kawnayn ila Shahadat al-Hasanayn, al-Tibyan fi Fada'il al-Nu'man, and al-Tibyan fi Hukm Shurb al-Dukhkhan. Most of it, rather all of it, is taken from my treatise: Tawrih al-Jinan bi Tashrih Hukm Shurb al-Dukhkhan, without acknowledgment. Some virtuous people were amazed when they saw his treatise, because it indicates the perfection of its author's erudition, breadth of vision, and vast knowledge. When they came across my treatise and knew that all the fatwas of scholars and investigations of virtuous people in it were taken from it, their amazement ceased and another amazement occurred to them, about taking from it without acknowledgment in any of its places. And he is an erudite scholar, a virtuous one encompassing every art. He acquired knowledge from the perfect ones of his time, including: our master Abd al-Hakim, author of Masir al-Da'ir Sharh al-Da'ir and Hawashi Sharh al-Sullam al-Hamd Allah and others - died in Safar of the year seven and eighty after one thousand and two hundred - son of our master Abd al-Rabb ibn Bahr al-Ulum, possessor of famous works. 134 Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. Then he went to the Haramayn, and after returning, he was appointed as a teacher at Madrasa Mirza, so he taught there for about fifteen years until he was dismissed in the year nine and ninety after one thousand and two hundred. Now he is retired in his homeland. 51. He is a jurist, worshiper, prophet, ascetic. He read portions of the curriculum books under al-Mufti Muhammad Asghar, and most of them under his son al-Mufti Yusuf (previously mentioned), in partnership with my deceased father. And he pledged allegiance to his maternal uncle our master Abd al-Wali, and obtained a share of his caliphate after his death in the year nine and seventy. He read some hadith books under our master Husayn Ahmad al-Mulihabadi, a student of Shah Abd al-Aziz al-Dihlawi. He authored Minhaj al-Ridwan fi Qiyam Ramadan, al-Anwar al-Ghaybiyya, and Hashiyat Sharh al-Wiqaya, not completed. Now he is occupied in performing the silsila; they enter into his pledge in the Qadiri silsila. 52. Among them: al-Mawlawi Muhammad Hasan ibn Zuhur Hasan ibn Shams Ali, from the progeny of Abdullah ibn Salam the Companion, from the people of Sanbhal, a town in the vicinity of Muradabad, student of his uncle al-Mufti Abd al-Salam al-Sanbhali, and al-Mawlawi Abd al-Karim Khan, and al-Mawlawi Sadid al-Din Khan al-Dihlawi, and al-Mawlawi Muhammad Qasim al-Nanawtawi. Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (Tarajim) listing Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries, super-commentaries, or annotations on Sharh al-Wiqaya, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh. The author, who is compiling these biographies, begins by mentioning a scholar whose lineage traces back to al-Qutb al-Shahid. He then details scholars numbered 50, 51, and 52, providing their full names, lineages, teachers, works, and sometimes death dates. Scholar 50 is al-Mawlawi al-Sayyid Abu al-Khayr Muhammad Mu'in al-Din al-Karwi, who wrote a commentary on the topic of intervening purity (al-tuhr al-mutakhalil) and many other works. The author notes that this scholar's treatise on smoking (shurb al-dukhan) was largely copied from the author's own treatise without acknowledgment, a point of curiosity among contemporary scholars. Scholar 51 is Muhammad Abd al-Razzaq, a jurist and ascetic who authored several works and initiated a Qadiri chain. Scholar 52 is Muhammad Hasan, a descendant of the Companion Abdullah ibn Salam, who studied under various teachers including Muhammad Qasim al-Nanawtawi. The passage ends with a reference to his death in 1304 AH. These biographies serve to establish the authority and chain of transmission for the commentaries on Sharh al-Wiqaya, a common practice in Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
تراجم (tarajim): Biographical notices of scholars
محشي (muhashshi): Commentator who writes marginal notes (hashiya) on a text
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqaya): A commentary on al-Wiqaya, a Hanafi fiqh text by Taju al-Shari'ah

Biographical list of Hanafi scholars and their works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of biographical sections in Hanafi legal texts and identify key scholars and their works mentioned in this passage.

Core Idea
Biographical chains establish authority and transmission in Hanafi scholarship.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents biographical sketches of Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries or glosses on Sharh al-Wiqaya, a central text in the Hanafi curriculum. Understanding these biographies helps you appreciate the scholarly lineage and the living tradition behind the legal rulings you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read each biography carefully and note the name, title (e.g., Mawlana, Mufti), and any geographical or lineage details.
The author often links scholars to teachers and earlier authorities.
2
Trace the Network
List the teachers and students mentioned. This reveals the chain of transmission (isnad) of Hanafi knowledge.
Notice names like Shah 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Dihlawi and Mulla Nizam al-Din – major figures in Indian Hanafism.
3
Record the Works
Identify any books or commentaries authored by the scholar. This shows their contribution to the Hanafi tradition.
Works like 'Hashiya Sharh al-Wiqaya' are glosses on the foundational text.
4

Observe any Sufi orders mentioned, such as the Qadiriyya, to understand the intellectual and spiritual context.
Many Hanafi scholars were also Sufis, blending fiqh with tasawwuf.
5

Connect each scholar's work to the central text Sharh al-Wiqaya and its tradition of commentary.
This passage is explicitly about 'commentators on Sharh al-Wiqaya'.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, listing notable Hanafi scholars. It begins with the biography of Mawlana 'Abd al-'Ali, a scholar from Madras, tracing his lineage to Mulla Nizam al-Din. It mentions his teaching at Lucknow and later at the Madrasa of Mirza Fur, and his retirement in 1299 AH. Then it lists other scholars: Mirza Hasan 'Ali al-Lakhnawi, a student of Shah 'Abd al-'Aziz; Mawlana Ni'mat Allah, the author's maternal uncle and teacher; Mawlana Mufti Zuhur Allah, his grandfather's grandfather and his teacher's teacher. Next is the biography of Mawlana Muhammad 'Abd al-Razzaq, a jurist and ascetic who studied under Mufti Muhammad Asghar and his son, and pledged allegiance to his maternal uncle 'Abd al-Wali. He authored several works, including a hashia on Sharh al-Wiqaya which remains incomplete. He was associated with the Qadiriyya spiritual chain. Finally, it mentions Mawlana Muhammad Hasan, a descendant of the Companion 'Abd Allah ibn Salam, who studied under various scholars and composed works on fara'id and a commentary on Khulasat al-Kaydani. The passage ends with a note on his death date and a reference to other biographical works. The text serves to establish the scholarly lineage and authority of the commentators on Sharh al-Wiqaya.

Key Terms
السلسلة القادرية (al-silsila al-qadiriyya): The Qadiriyya spiritual order (tariqa) named after 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani.
محدث (muhaddith): A scholar specialized in hadith sciences.
حاشية شرح الوقاية (hashiyat sharh al-wiqaya): A gloss or supercommentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya, a standard Hanafi legal text.

The Scholar's Autobiography: Establishing Authority in Hanafi Tradition
Autobiographical introduction by the author of a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and key elements of a traditional Hanafi scholar's autobiography (tarjama) and identify how such details establish scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's autobiography is a chain of authority (sanad) that gives weight to his rulings.

In classical Hanafi works, authors often include a personal biography (tarjama) not as vanity but as a credential. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya introduces the author, 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, detailing his birth, Quran memorization, and education under his father. Understanding this tradition helps you place the author's work within the Hanafi lineage and evaluate the reliability of his teachings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his humility
The author calls himself 'al-ʿabd al-ḍaʿīf' (the weak servant). This is a standard trope of humility, but it also signals his awareness of his place in the scholarly tradition.
Note the contrast with the authority he later claims through his teachers and works.
2
List the key biographical details
Extract the date and place of birth (26 Dhul Qaʿda 1264 AH / Bandah), the age of Quran memorization (start at 5, finish at 10), and the curriculum studied under his father.
These details form the sanad (chain) of his learning, which is crucial for Hanafi authority.
3
Understand the purpose of the biography
The author states he wrote this introduction so that 'those who do not know me may know me and pray for me'. Beyond this, it serves to authenticate his scholarly lineage and situate his work within the tradition.
Autobiographies are often linked to previous works (e.g., al-Nafiʿ al-Kabir) to create a cohesive scholarly identity.

Biography of the weak servant describing this authorship. I have mentioned something of my condition in 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir li man Yutali' al-Jami' al-Saghir', and in 'al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyya 'ala al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya'(2), and in the introduction to 'al-Si'aya'(3), and in the introduction to 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad', to be a reminder for me in my life and after my death. I was born on the 26th of Dhu al-Qa'da, Tuesday, in the year 1264 AH, in the town of Bandah, when my deceased father was a teacher there. I occupied myself with memorizing the Noble Quran from when I was about five years old, and finished it when I was ten years old. During that time I also read some Persian books and other things. After finishing the memorization – and that was in Jaunpur, when my deceased father was a teacher there – I began pursuing the Arabic sciences under the guidance of my deceased father, and I read the standard books from 'Mizan al-Sarf' to 'Tafsir al-Baydawi' and 'al-Qadima'? all upon him.

Commentary
This passage is an autobiography by the author, 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi? (the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya). He introduces himself as a humble servant and lists some of his previous works where he has mentioned his life, such as 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir' and introductions to other commentaries. He then provides specific details: his birth on 26 Dhu al-Qa'da 1264 AH (1848 CE) in Bandah, where his father was a teacher. The text breaks off mid-sentence, but it indicates the author's thorough traditional education. This biography establishes the author's credentials as a Hanafi scholar and is typical in Islamic works to provide authority and context.

The Scholar’s Formation: Dars Nizami and Ijazah in the Hanafi Tradition
A scholar’s autobiographical biography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the Dars Nizami curriculum and explain the function of ijazah in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A classical Hanafi scholar’s training was a structured journey from Quran memorization to comprehensive mastery, culminating in an ijazah connecting him to the Prophet.

This lesson examines the author's autobiographical account from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, which offers a window into the classical Hanafi educational system. The passage details the Dars Nizami curriculum—a twelve-year program of Arabic sciences, logic, fiqh, and other disciplines—and the authorization (ijazah) that links a scholar to earlier authorities. Understanding this background is essential for appreciating how Hanafi fiqh texts were transmitted and why certain scholars carry authoritative weight.

Guided Path
1
Outline the author’s education timeline
The author memorized the Quran from age 5 to 10, then studied the Dars Nizami curriculum under his father until age 17. Identify these milestones and their significance.
Note that memorization of Quran was the foundation.
2
Identify the curriculum structure
List the subjects and books mentioned: morphology, grammar, rhetoric, logic, wisdom, fiqh, usul, hadith, tafsir, mathematics, etc. Note for each the first and last book cited.
This curriculum is the Dars Nizami, standardized in India.
3
Recognize the role of teachers
The author studied almost all sciences with his father, and after his father’s death, mathematics with his uncle. Note the emphasis on learning from a single master for foundational subjects.
Personal transmission was key.
4
Understand the function of ijazah
His father granted him ijazah (authorization) in all sciences, citing three teachers in the chain: Shaykh Jamal al-Hanafi, Shaykh Muhammad al-Gharb al-Shafi’i, and Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghani al-Dihlawi. Explain why ijazah is crucial for authenticity.
Ijazah ensures unbroken chains of transmission (sanad).
5
Connect to Hanafi tradition
Reflect on how this biography shows the integration of transmitted (manqul) and rational (ma‘qul) sciences in Hanafi scholarship, and how ijazah links the author to earlier authorities across madhhabs.
The chain includes Hanafi, Shafi‘i, and other scholars, showing scholarly interconnectedness.

وثانيتهما : الرحلة من حيدر آباد إلى الحرمين الشريفين.
عمري
ولم أقرأ شيئاً من الكتب العلمية على غير الوالد إلا بعض كتب علم الرياضي ک شروح التذكرة للبرْجَنْدي وللخفري وللسيد السند، و«رسالة الاسطرلاب» للطوسي، و«زيج الغ بيكس» مع شرحه للبرْجَنْدِي، وزيج بهادر خاني»، و«رسالة في النجوم»، فقد قرأتها بعد وفاته على خالِهِ وأستاذه مولانا محمد نعمت الله المرحوم ، صاحب اليد الطولى في العلوم الرياضية ، وأنا آخر من تلمذ عليه.
وقد رأيت في المنام في تلك الأيام المحقق نصير الدين الطوسي، مؤلّف «التذكرة»، و«التجريد»، و«تحرير إقليدس»، وغيرها، وسألته عن أشياء، وأثنى علي بالاشتغال بهذا الفنّ، وأظهر الفرح والسرور وبشرني بحصول الكمال في هذا الفن.
1. وقد أجازني الوالد بجميع العلوم:
عن الشيخ جمال الحنفي المكي، تلميذ المفتي عبد الله السراج.
وعن الشيخ . محمد بن محمد الغرب الشافعي، المدرس في المسجد النبوي. وعن الشيخ عبد الغني الدهلوي، تلميذ الشيخ عابد السندي، مؤلّف «حصر الشارد».
والشمس البازغة للجونبوري
وفي الرياضية: «خلاصة الحساب» باب التصحيح، والمقالة الأولى من تحرير الإقليدس»، و«تشريح الأفلاك»، و«القوشجية»، والباب الأول من شرح الجغميني».
وفي الفقه : النصف الأول من شرح الوقاية»، والنصف الثاني من «هداية الفقه». وفي أصول الفقه : «نور الأنوار»، و«التلويح» إلى المقدمات الأربع ، و(مسلم الثبوت» إلى المبادئ الكلامية.
وفي الكلام: «شرح العقائد للتفتازاني إلى السمعيات، والجزء الأول من «شرح العقائد» للدواني ، و میر زاهد شرح المواقف مبحث الأمور العامة.
وفي التفسير الجلالين»، و«البيضاوي» إلى آخر سورة البقرة.
وفي الحديث : «مشكاة المصابيح» إلى كتاب الجمعة.
وفي المناظرة : «الرشيدية». ينظر : معارف العوارف» (ص (١٦) ، و(المنهج الفقهي» (ص٤٨ - ٤٩).
The eighth study: Biographies of the annotators of Sharh al-Wiqayah. 135 He is a virtuous, complete person, well-prepared. He authored a solid matn in the science of fara'id, and 'Sharh Khulasat al-Kaydani'. He mentioned to me that his birth was in Sha'ban of the year sixty-four, and that he authored 'Hashiyat Sharh al-Wiqayah', of which he has written about seventy parts so far. 53. Biography of the weak slave [the author] describing this composition. I have mentioned some of my condition in 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir li-man Yutali' al-Jami' al-Saghir', and in 'al-Ta'liqat al-Sunniyah 'ala al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyah', and in the introduction of 'al-Si'ayah', and in the introduction of 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Muhammad' to be a reminder for me in my life and after my death. And I mention here a necessary amount so that he who does not know me may know me, and pray for me with good beginning and end. I was born on the 26th of Dhu al-Qa'dah, Tuesday, year 1264 AH, in the town of Bandeh, while my deceased father was a teacher there. I engaged in memorizing the Noble Quran from when I was about five years old, and finished it when I was ten years old, and during that I read some Persian books and others. After I finished memorization – and that was in Jaunpur, when my deceased father was a teacher there – I began acquiring the Arabic sciences under the care of the deceased father, and I read the prescribed books from 'Mizan al-Sarf' to 'Tafsir al-Baydawi' and 'al-Qadimah' all upon him. (0)~~ (1) al-Nafi' al-Kabir (pp. 60-66). (2) al-Ta'liqat al-Sunniyah (pp. 421-422). (3) Introduction to al-Si'ayah (pp. 41-42). (4) Introduction to al-Ta'liq (1:109-133). (5) That is, in the systematic curriculum which was taught in twelve years, and a summary of what is studied in it from sciences and books are as follows: In morphology: 'al-Mizan', 'al-Munsha'ib', 'Yadh Kunj', 'Zubdah', 'Sarf Mir', 'al-Fusul al-Akbariyah', 'al-Shafiyah'. In grammar: 'al-Nahw Mir', 'Sharh al-Mi'ah', 'Hidayat al-Nahw', 'al-Kafiyah', 'Sharh al-Kafiyah li al-Jami ila mabhath al-hal'. In rhetoric: 'al-Mukhtasar', 'al-Mutawwal'. In logic: 'al-Sughra', 'al-Kubra', 'al-Isaghuji', 'al-Tahdhib', 'Sharh al-Tahdhib', 'Qutbi', 'Mir Qutbi', 'Sullam al-'Ulum', 'Mir Zahid Risalah', 'Mir Zahid Mulla Jalal'. In wisdom: 'Sharh Hidayat al-Hikmah li al-Maizi', and its commentary by al-Sadr al-Shirazi up to the chapter on place. [PAGE_136] 136 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah and 'al-Nafisi' and 'al-Shams al-Bazighah' and other books of Hadith, Tafsir, Fiqh, Usul, and the rest of transmitted and rational books. I finished my studies when I was seventeen years old, with interruptions due to two journeys: one: the journey from homeland to Hyderabad Deccan. The second: the journey from Hyderabad to the two noble Harams. And I did not read any scientific books from anyone other than my father except some mathematical books such as the commentaries on 'al-Tadhkirah' by al-Birjandi, al-Khafri, and al-Sayyid al-Sind, and 'Risalah al-Asturlab' by al-Tusi, and 'Zij Ulugh Beg' with its commentary by al-Birjandi, and 'Zij Bahadur Khani', and 'Risalah fi al-Nujum'. I read these after his death from his maternal uncle and teacher Maulana Muhammad Ni'mat Allah al-Marhum, the one with great skill in mathematical sciences, and I am the last who studied under him. I saw in a dream in those days the investigator Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, author of 'al-Tadhkirah', 'al-Tajrid', 'Tahrir Uqlidis', and others, and I asked him about things, and he praised me for engaging in this art, and showed joy and happiness, and gave me glad tidings of perfection in this art. 1. My father granted me authorization (ijazah) in all sciences: from Shaykh Jamal al-Hanafi al-Makki, student of Mufti 'Abd Allah al-Siraj. And from Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Gharb al-Shafi'i, teacher in the Prophet's Mosque. And from Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Dihlawi, student of Shaykh 'Abid al-Sindi, author of 'Hasr al-Sharid'. And al-Shams al-Bazighah li al-Jawnburi. And in mathematics: 'Khulasat al-Hisab' chapter on correction, and the first article of 'Tahrir Uqlidis', and 'Tashrih al-Aflak', and 'al-Qushjiyah', and the first chapter of 'Sharh al-Jaghmini'. And in fiqh: the first half of 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and the second half of 'Hidayat al-Fiqh'. And in usul al-fiqh: 'Nur al-Anwar', and 'al-Talwih' up to the four introductions, and 'Musallam al-Thubut' up to the theological principles. And in kalam: 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id li al-Taftazani up to the sam'iyyat, and the first part of 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id li al-Dawani, and Mir Zahid's commentary on 'al-Mawaqif' section on general matters. And in tafsir: 'al-Jalalayn' and 'al-Baydawi' up to the end of Surat al-Baqarah. And in hadith: 'Mishkat al-Masabih' up to the book of Jumu'ah. And in munazara: 'al-Rashidiyyah'. See: Ma'arif al-'Awarif (p. 16) and al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi (pp. 48-49).
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account by the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah', where he describes his own life, scholarly journey, and teachers. It begins with a brief description of a virtuous scholar (possibly al-Muhashshi or another figure) who authored a matn on fara'id and a commentary, and then transitions to the author's own biography. The author provides his birth details: 26th Dhu al-Qa'dah, 1264 AH (around 1848 CE) in Bandeh. He started memorizing the Quran at age five and finished at ten, also reading Persian books. After moving to Jaunpur with his father (a teacher), he studied the standard curriculum (Dars Nizami) under his father, covering morphology, grammar, rhetoric, logic, wisdom, and more. He completed his studies at age seventeen, with interruptions due to travel to Hyderabad and then to the Haramayn. He further studied mathematics under his maternal uncle after his father's death. He mentions a dream of Nasir al-Din al-Tusi who encouraged him. His ijazah chain includes Shaykh Jamal al-Hanafi al-Makki, Shaykh Muhammad al-Gharb al-Shafi'i, and Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Dihlawi. The passage lists many books he studied in various disciplines. This is a standard scholarly biography (tarjamah) that establishes the author's credentials and lineage of knowledge.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Scholarly authorization to transmit or teach books and sciences.
الدرس النظامي (al-dars al-nizami): The standardized curriculum taught in Indian madrasas, usually spanning twelve years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what age did the author complete the Dars Nizami curriculum (formal studies)?
A) 10 years
B) 12 years
C) 17 years
D) 20 years

Key Takeaway
The author’s biography demonstrates that a classical Hanafi scholar's authority rests on a structured curriculum (Dars Nizami) and an unbroken chain of authorization (ijazah), ensuring authentic transmission of knowledge.

Life of the Author
beginner
6 min
The Scholarly Journey of the Author of Umdat al-Ri'ayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key stages of the author's education, list his primary teachers, and explain the significance of ijazah in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is built through a chain of teachers (isnad) and formal ijazat.

This biography from the introduction of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' introduces the author's credentials. Understanding his scholarly lineage helps us evaluate the work's authority. The passage details his early completion of studies, his teachers (especially his father), his dream of Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, the ijazat he received, and his own prolific authorship.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's early education
The author studied primarily under his father and completed his studies by age 17, with interruptions for travel to Hyderabad Deccan and the two sanctuaries.
He began teaching and writing from youth.
2
Identify the breadth of subjects studied
He studied tafsir, hadith, fiqh, usul, kalam, mathematics, and more, as evidenced by the list of books and commentaries.
The list includes both transmitted (manqul) and rational (ma'qul) sciences.
3
Examine the ijazat (scholarly licenses)
The author received ijazat from multiple teachers: his father, Shaykh Jamal al-Hanafi al-Makki, Shaykh Muhammad al-Gharb al-Shafi'i, Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Dihlawi, Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i, and others.
These ijazat connect him to earlier authorities.
4
Analyze the dream of Nasir al-Din al-Tusi
The author saw al-Tusi in a dream, who praised his engagement in mathematics and gave glad tidings of perfection. This serves as a spiritual endorsement.
Dreams are sometimes used in biographies to highlight divine favor or motivation.
5
Review the list of authored works
The author lists his works in morphology, grammar, logic, philosophy, and other fields, noting that some remain incomplete.
Many are commentaries or glosses, showing his engagement with earlier texts.

My age: I did not read any scholarly books under anyone other than my father, except some books of mathematics such as commentaries on al-Tadhkirah by al-Barjandi, al-Khafri, and al-Sayyid al-Sanad, and 'Risalah al-Usturlab' by al-Tusi, and 'Zij al-Ulughbek' with its commentary by al-Barjandi, and 'Zij Bahadur Khani', and 'Risalah fi al-Nujum'. In those days, I saw in a dream the investigator Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, author of 'al-Tadhkirah', 'al-Tajrid', 'Tahrir Uqlidis', and others. I asked him about things, and he praised my engagement in this art, showed joy and happiness, and gave me glad tidings of attaining perfection in this art. 1. My father granted me ijazah in all sciences: from Shaykh Jamal al-Hanafi al-Makki, student of Mufti 'Abd Allah al-Siraj; from Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Gharb al-Shafi'i, teacher in the Prophet's Mosque; from Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Dihlawi, student of Shaykh 'Abid al-Sindi, author of 'Hasr al-Sharid'. And in fiqh: the first half of 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and the second half of 'Hidayat al-Fiqh'. And in usul al-fiqh: 'Nur al-Anwar', and 'al-Talwih' up to the four introductory chapters, and 'Musallam al-Thubut' up to the theological principles. In kalam: 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id' by al-Taftazani up to al-Sam'iyyat, and the first part of 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id' by al-Dawani, and Mir Zahid's 'Sharh al-Mawaqif' section on general matters. In tafsir: 'al-Jalalayn' and 'al-Baydawi' up to the end of Surah al-Baqarah. In hadith: 'Mishkat al-Masabih' up to the Book of Jumu'ah. In munazarah: 'al-Rashidiyyah'. See: 'Ma'arif al-'Awarif' (p. 16) and 'al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi' (pp. 48-49). And from Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i. And from other teachers as recorded in his ijazah document. He also granted me ijazah when I entered the two noble sanctuaries the first time with my honorable parents: Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i from his teachers as recorded in his chain document. Also, in that journey, Shaykh al-Dala'il 'Ali al-Hariri al-Madani granted me ijazah in early Muharram of the year 80. 4. Also, the Hanbali mufti in Makkah, our master Sayyid Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Humaid, who died in 95 [AH]; I met him during the second journey when I entered the two sanctuaries in 92 [AH]. 5. Also, Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Marhum, on the authority of Shaykh 'Abid al-Sindi and other teachers of his. And Allah enabled me to engage in teaching and authorship from the prime of youth, even from childhood. Allah's blessings upon me from the beginning are countless. So I authored: [1] In morphology: 'al-Tibyan sharh al-Mizan', and 'Takmilat al-Mizan' and its commentary, and 'Imtihan al-Talabah fi al-Siyagh al-Mushkilah', and another treatise named 'Jarkul'. [6][7] 2. In grammar: 'Khair al-Kalam fi Tashih Kalam al-Muluk Muluk al-Kalam', and 'Izzalah al-Jamad 'an I'rab Akmal al-Hamd'. [A]. In munazarah: 'al-Hadiyyah al-Mukhtariyyah sharh al-Risalah al-'Adudiyyah'. 4. In logic and philosophy: an old gloss on the notes of Ghulam Yahya al-Bahari relating to the glosses of al-Zahid on 'al-Risalah al-Qutbiyyah' called 'Hidayat al-Wara', and a second gloss on it called 'Misbah al-Duja', and a third gloss on it called 'Nur al-Huda', and 'al-Ta'liq al-'Ajib li-Hall Hashiyat al-Jalal 'ala al-Tahdhib', and 'Hall al-Mughlaq fi Bahth al-Majhul al-Mutlaq', and 'al-Kalam al-Matin fi Tahrir al-Barahin'. And 'Maysar al-'Asir fi Bahth al-Muthanna bi al-Takrir', and 'al-Ifadah al-Khatirah fi Bahth Sab' 'Ard Sha'irah', and 'Takmilat Hashiyat al-Walid al-Marhum 'ala al-Nafisi', and 'Daf' al-Kilal 'an Tullab Ta'liqat al-Kamal', and 'al-Ma'arif bima fi Hawashi Sharh al-Mawaqif', and 'Ta'liq al-Hama'il 'ala Hawashi al-Zahid 'ala Sharh al-Hayakil', and 'Hashiyat Badi' al-Mizan', and these four have not been completed up to this time.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah'. The author provides a detailed account of his scholarly journey, including his teachers, the books he studied, and his own works. He studied primarily under his father but also learned mathematics from his maternal uncle after his father's death. He had a dream vision of Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, which encouraged him. He received multiple ijazat (scholarly licenses) from prominent scholars, including Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i and the Hanbali mufti of Makkah. The author then lists his own works in various disciplines: morphology, grammar, logic, philosophy, and other fields. Many of these works are commentaries or glosses on earlier texts. The passage ends by noting that four of his works remain incomplete. This biography establishes the author's credentials and scholarly lineage, which is typical for a hashya (super-commentary). The fact that he authored so many works and began teaching at a young age highlights his erudition.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): A scholarly license or certification to transmit knowledge, often with a chain of teachers.
الوالد (al-walid): The author's father, who was his primary teacher and granted him ijazah in all sciences.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): A commentary on the Hanafi fiqh text 'al-Wiqayah' by Taju al-Shari'ah. The author studied the first half of this commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From whom did the author primarily receive his ijazah in all sciences?
A) His maternal uncle
B) His father
C) Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan
D) Nasir al-Din al-Tusi

Key Takeaway
The author's extensive education under his father and other scholars, combined with multiple ijazat, establishes his authority to produce a major Hanafi commentary.

The Scholarly Lineage and Works of the Annotator of Sharh al-Wiqayah
Biographical listing of teachers and authored works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ijazah in the Hanafi tradition and list the major works of the annotator of Sharh al-Wiqayah across different disciplines.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is preserved through continuous chains of ijazah, ensuring the accurate transmission of knowledge.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah introduces the author's credentials by naming his teachers and cataloguing his scholarly output. Understanding this biography helps you appreciate the rigorous tradition of learning and teaching in the Hanafi school, where knowledge is transmitted through formal permission (ijazah) from qualified masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his teachers
Read the beginning of the passage to list the teachers mentioned, noting their madhhabs and the cities where the author studied.
Teachers include al-Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan (Shafi'i), 'Ali al-Hariri al-Madani, and Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Humayd (Hanbali).
2
Understand the concept of ijazah
Note how the author received ijazah from each teacher, and how this license authenticates his authority to teach and write.
Ijazah is a formal chain linking the student to earlier authorities, ensuring the preservation of accurate transmission.
3
Catalog the author's works by discipline
Scan the list of authored works and group them by field: morphology (sarf), grammar (nahw), disputation, logic, biography, fiqh, etc.
The author wrote commentaries (shuruh), glosses (hawashi), and independent treatises.
4
Recognize the importance of biographical works
Observe that the author compiled several biographical dictionaries (tarajim), including one specifically on Hanafi scholars (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah).
Such works preserve the chains of transmission and scholarly heritage of the Hanafi school.

The eighth study: Biographies of the annotator of Sharh al-Wiqayah. And from al-Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i. And from other teachers as recorded in his license page. And also in that journey, Shaykh al-Dala'il 'Ali al-Hariri al-Madani granted me permission at the beginning of Muharram of the year eighty. 4. Also the Hanbali mufti in Mecca, our master al-Sayyid Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Humayd, who died in the year ninety-five; I met him in the second journey when I entered the two noble sanctuaries in the year ninety-two. 5. Also al-Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Marhum, from al-Shaykh 'Abid al-Sindi and other teachers. And Allah enabled me to engage in teaching and authorship from the prime of youth, indeed from childhood, and Allah's blessings upon me from the beginning are countless. So I authored: 1. In the science of morphology: al-Tibyan fi Sharh al-Mizan, and Takmilat al-Mizan, and its commentary, and Imtihan al-Talabah fi al-Siyagh al-Mushkila, and another treatise named 'Jarkal'. 2. In the science of grammar: Khayr al-Kalam fi Tashih Kalam al-Muluk Muluk al-Kalam, and Izalat al-Jamad 'an I'rab Akmal al-Hamd. 3. In the science of disputation: al-Hadiyat al-Mukhtariyyah fi Sharh al-Risalah al-'Adudiyyah. 4. In logic and philosophy: an old commentary on the glosses of Ghulam Yahya al-Bahari related to the glosses of al-Zahid on al-Risalah al-Qutbiyyah named Hidayah al-Wara, a second gloss on it named Misbah al-Duja, a third gloss on it named Nur al-Huda, and al-Ta'liq al-'Ajib li Hall Hashiyat al-Jalal 'ala al-Tahdhib, and Hall al-Mughlaq fi Bahth al-Majhul al-Mutlaq, and al-Kalam al-Matin fi Tahrir al-Barahin. Also: Maysar al-'Asir fi Bahth al-Muthanna bi al-Takrir, and al-Ifadat al-Khatirah fi Bahth Sab' 'Ard Sha'irah, and Takmilat Hashiyat al-Walid al-Marhum 'ala al-Nafisi, and Daf' al-Kalal 'an Tullab Ta'liqat al-Kamal, and al-Ma'arif bi ma fi Hawashi Sharh al-Mawaqif, and Ta'liq al-Hama'il 'ala Hawashi al-Zahid 'ala Sharh al-Hayakil, and Hashiyat Badi' al-Mizan, but these four have not been completed until this time. In the science of biographies and history: Husr al-'Alam bi Wafat Marji' al-'Alam, and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyyah, and (4) al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyyah, and Muqaddimat al-Hidayah and its appendix named Mudhayylat al-Dirayah, and Muqaddimat al-Jami' al-Saghir named al-Nafi' al-Kabir, and Muqaddimat al-Si'ayah, and Muqaddimat al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad. These three together are named Inba' al-Khullan bi Abna' 'Ulama' Hindustan, not yet completed. And Ibriz al-Ghayy al-Waqi' fi Shifa' al-'Ayy. 6. In the science of fiqh, siyar, hadith, and others: al-Hashiyah al-Qadimah li Sharh al-Wiqayah, and its commentary named al-Si'ayah fi Kashf ma fi Sharh al-Wiqayah, not yet completed until this hour, and this third commentary named 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, and (38) al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' al-Imam Muhammad, and Jam' al-Ghurrar fi al-Radd 'ala Nathr al-Durar, in which I replied to those who refuted some points related to the phrase of 'al-Tafhimat' found in the treatise of my late father, named Nazm al-Durar fi Silki Shaqq al-Qamar. And al-Qawl al-Ashraf fi al-Fath 'an al-Mushaf, and al-Qawl al-Manshur fi Hilal Khayr al-Shuhur, and its gloss named al-Qawl al-Manthur, and Zajr Arbab al-Rayan 'an Shurb al-Dukhan, which I made into a part of another treatise named Tawrih al-Jinan bi Tashrih Hukm Shurb al-Dukhan. And al-Insaf fi Hukm al-I'tikaf, and al-Ifsah 'an Hukm Shahadat al-Mar'ah fi al-Irda', and Tuhfat al-Talabah fi Mash al-Ruqabah, and its gloss named Tuhfat al-Kamilah, and Sibat al-Fikr fi al-Jahr bi al-Dhikr, and Ihkam al-Qantarah fi Ahkam al-Basmalah, and (5) Ghayat al-Maqal fi ma Yata'allaq bi al-Ni'al, and its gloss named Zafar al-Anfal. Al-Hashasah bi Naqd al-Wudu' bi al-Qahqahah, and Khayr al-Khabar bi Adhan Khayr al-Bashar, and Raf' al-Sitr 'an Kayfiyyat Idkhal al-Mayyit wa Tawjihihi fi al-Qabr, and Qut al-Mughtadin bi Fath (1) Occurred in the original: yufrad.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, detailing the scholarly life of the annotator (muhashshi) of Sharh al-Wiqayah. It lists his teachers, his travels to Mecca and Medina, and his extensive authored works across various Islamic sciences. The passage serves as an introduction to the author's credentials, emphasizing his permission (ijazah) from prominent scholars of different madhhabs: Shafi'i, Hanbali, and others. His teachers include al-Sayyid Ahmad Dahlan al-Shafi'i, 'Ali al-Hariri al-Madani, Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Humayd (Hanbali mufti of Mecca), and 'Abd al-Ghani al-Sindi. The author then lists his own works in morphology (sarf), grammar (nahw), disputation (munazarah), logic and philosophy (mantiq wa hikmah), biography (tarajim), history, fiqh, siyar (prophetic biographies), hadith, and other topics. Notable works include commentaries and glosses on classic Hanafi texts, such as his commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah (al-Si'ayah) and the present work 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. He also authored works on contemporary issues like smoking (shurb al-dukhan) and legal rulings on i'tikaf, shahadah, and istinja. The passage reflects the scholarly output of a well-trained Hanafi jurist who engaged in teaching, writing, and debate across multiple disciplines.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Scholarly license or permission to teach a particular text or field, granted by a teacher to a student.
تراجم (tarajim): Biographies; here it refers to the author's work compiling biographies of Hanafi scholars and others.
المقدمة (muqaddimah): An introduction to a book; the author notes that even though introductions are part of the book, they are counted separately due to their independent value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The annotator of Sharh al-Wiqayah was a highly trained Hanafi scholar who obtained ijazah from multiple teachers across madhhabs and authored numerous works, especially in fiqh and Hanafi biography.

The Scholarly Legacy of Imam al-Lakhnawi: A Catalogue of Works
Author enumerates his numerous scholarly works across disciplines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major works of Imam al-Lakhnawi across tarajim, fiqh, hadith, and other sciences, and explain the significance of his third hashiah 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah'.

Core Idea
Imam al-Lakhnawi authored over 50 works across multiple Islamic sciences, demonstrating the ideal of comprehensive Hanafi scholarship.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' presents a remarkable catalogue of works by its author, Imam 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi. Far from being a dry list, it reveals the breadth of Hanafi scholarship in 19th-century India and the author's dedication to serving the madhhab through commentaries, treatises, and biographical works. By examining this list, you will gain insight into the scholarly output of a major Hanafi authority and the types of writings valued in the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fields covered
Scan the passage for explicit mentions of disciplines: tarajim (biographies), fiqh (jurisprudence), siyar (prophetic biography), hadith, and others. Note the specific terms used.
The author groups his works under these headings, showing his specialization.
2
Locate works on tarajim
Find the titles listed under 'In the science of biographies and history'. Note which are completed and which remain unfinished (e.g., 'Inba' al-Khillan' not yet completed).
These works form part of his legacy in preserving Hanafi scholarly heritage.
3
Examine the hashiyas on Sharh al-Wiqayah
Identify the three hashiyas mentioned: al-Hashiyah al-Qadimah, al-Si'ayah (unfinished), and the present work 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. Understand their chronological order and purpose.
The third hashiah is the one you are currently studying.
4
Survey the variety of other works
Read through the list of titles on diverse topics: from i'tikaf to smoking, from women's testimony to recitation behind an imam. Observe the range.
This shows the author's engagement with contemporary issues and classical fiqh.
5
Note the author's gratitude and editorial footnotes
Read the concluding sentence thanking Allah for acceptance, and the two footnotes confirming the widespread recognition of his works. This provides context for his authority.
The footnotes also reference a separate work detailing al-Lakhnawi's life and works.

وفي علم التراجم والتاريخ : حسرة العالم بوفاة مرجع العالم، والفوائد البهية في تراجم الحنفية، والتعليقات السنية، ومقدمة الهداية وذيله المسمى بـ مذيلة الدراية، ومقدمة الجامع الصغير المسماة بـ النافع الكبير، ومقدمة السعاية، ومقدمة التعليق الممجد. ومقدمة عمدة الرعاية التي نحن بصدد تأليفها، وهاتان المقدمتان وإن كانتا مدرجتين في الكتاب، لكنّهما لمشابهتهما لغيرها حق أن يفردا بالتعداد، وخير العمل بذكر تراجم علماء فرنجي محل، والنصيب الأوفر في تراجم علماء المئة الثالثة عشر، ورسالة أخرى في تراجم السابقين من علماء الهند، وهذه الثلاثة مجموعها المسمى بـ إنباء الخلان بأبناء علماء هندوستان ولم يتم إلى الآن، وإبراز الغي الواقع في شفاء العي. وفي علم الفقه والسير والحديث، وغير ذلك : الحاشية القديمة لشرح الوقاية، وشرحه المسمى بـ السعاية في كشف ما في شرح الوقاية، ولم يتم إلى هذه الساعة، وهذه الحاشية الثالثة المسماة بـ عمدة الرعاية، والتعليق الممجّد على موطأ الإمام محمد، وجمع الغرر في الرد على نثر الدرر، رددت فيه على من ردّ على بعض المواضع المتعلّق بعبارة التفهيمات الواقع في رسالة الوالد المرحوم، المسماة بـ نظم الدرر في سلك شق القمر. والقول الأشرف في الفتح عن المصحف، والقول المنشور في هلال خير الشهور، وتعليقه المسمى بـ القول المنثور، وزجر أرباب الريان عن شرب الدخان وقد جعلته جزءاً لرسالة أخرى مسمّاة بـ ترويح الجنان بتشريح حكم شرب الدخان. والإنصاف في حكم الاعتكاف، والإفصاح عن حكم شهادة المرأة في الإرضاع، وتحفة الطلبة في مسح الرقبة، وتعليقه المسمّى بـ تحفة الكملة، وسباحة الفكر في الجهر بالذكر، وإحكام القنطرة في أحكام البسملة، وغاية المقال فيما يتعلّق بالنعال، وتعليقه المسمّى بـ ظفر الأنفال. الهسهسة بنقض الوضوء بالقهقهة، وخير الخبر بأذان خير البشر، ورفع الستر عن كيفية إدخال الميت وتوجيهه في القبر، وقوت المغتدين بفتح المقتدين، وإفادة الخير في الاستياك بسواك الغير، والتحقيق العجيب في التثويب، والكلام الجليل فيما يتعلّق بالمنديل. وتحفة الأخيار في إحياء سنة سيّد الأبرار، وتعليقه المسمّى بـ نخبة الأنظار، وإقامة الحجة على أنّ الإكثار في التعبد ليس ببدعة، وتحفة النبلاء فيما يتعلق بجماعة النساء، وزجر الناس على إنكار أثر ابن عباس، والفلك الدوار فيما يتعلّق برؤية الهلال بالنهار، والفلك المشحون في الأجوبة الكاملة للأسئلة العشرة الكاملة، وانتفاع الراهن والمرتهن بالمرهون، وظفر الأماني بشرح المختصر المنسوب إلى الجرجاني ولم يتم إلى الآن، وإمام الكلام فيما يتعلق بالقراءة خلف الإمام، وتعليقه المسمى بـ تعليق الفوائد العظام. وتدوير الفلك في حصول الجماعة بالجن والملك، ونزهة الفكر في سبحة الذكر وتعليقه المسمّى بـ النفحة، والقول الجازم في سقوط الحد بنكاح المحارم، وآكام النفائس في أداء الأذكار بلسان الفارس، وتحفة الثقات في تفاضل اللغات، ولم تتم إلى هذه الأوقات. وردع الإخوان عما أحدثوه في آخر جمعة رمضان، ورسالة في الغيبة ولم تتم، ورسالة في الأحاديث الموضوعة ولم تتم، وتبصرة البصائر في معرفة الأواخر ولم تتم، وجمع المواعظ الحسنة لخطب شهور السنة، البينات على وجود الأنبياء في الطبقات. ودافع الوسواس في أثر ابن عباس لله، والكلام المبرم في نقض القول المحكم، والكلام المبرور في ردّ القول المنصور، والسعي المشكور في ردّ المذهب المأثور، هداية المغتذين في فتح المقتدين، وغير ذلك. وإني أشكر الله شكراً متوالياً على أن رزق لتصانيفي قبولاً عالياً، وجعلها محمودةً بألسنة الطلبة والكملة، ورزقها شيوعاً تاماً، واشتهاراً عاماً، حتى توجهت إليها الأفاضل من الديار البعيدة والأمصار الشاسعة.
(۱) تكلمت عن مؤلفات الإمام اللكنوي بالتفصيل وصحة نسبتها إليها وضبط أسمائها وعددها في كتاب أفردته بترجمته وسميته المنهج الفقهي للإمام الكنوي، ففيه كفاية لكل مستزيد، ولا حاجة هنا للإعادة.
(٢) إننا إلى يومنا هذا ما زلنا نلحظ القبول العجيب لمؤلفات الإمام اللكنوي، والرضى بتحقيقاته
And in the science of biographies and history: 'Husrat al-'Alam bi Wafat Marji' al-'Alam', and 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyyah', and 'al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyyah', and 'Muqaddimat al-Hidayah' and its appendix called 'Mudhayyilat al-Dirayah', and 'Muqaddimat al-Jami' al-Saghir' named 'al-Nafi' al-Kabir', and 'Muqaddimat al-Si'ayah', and 'Muqaddimat al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad'. And 'Muqaddimat 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' which we are engaged in composing; these two introductions, although included in the book, due to their similarity to others deserve to be counted separately, and the best deed is mentioning the biographies of the scholars of Farangi Mahal, and 'al-Nasib al-Awfar fi Tarajim 'Ulama' al-Mi'ah al-Thalithat 'Ashar', and another treatise on the biographies of the earlier scholars of India - these three together are called 'Inba' al-Khillan bi Abna' 'Ulama' Hindustan' but not yet completed, and 'Ibriz al-Ghay al-Waqi' fi Shifa' al-'Ayy'. And in the sciences of fiqh, siyar, and hadith, and others: 'al-Hashiyah al-Qadimah li Sharh al-Wiqayah', and its commentary called 'al-Si'ayah fi Kashf ma fi Sharh al-Wiqayah', not completed up to now, and this third hashiah called ''Umdat al-Ri'ayah', and 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' al-Imam Muhammad', and 'Jam' al-Ghurar fi al-Radd 'ala Nathr al-Durar', in which I refuted whoever objected to some points related to the expression of 'al-Tafhimat' occurring in the treatise of my late father, called 'Nazm al-Durar fi Silki Shaqq al-Qamar'. And 'al-Qawl al-Ashraf fi al-Fath 'an al-Mushaf', and 'al-Qawl al-Manshur fi Hilal Khayr al-Shuhur', and its commentary called 'al-Qawl al-Manthur', and 'Zajr Arbab al-Rayyan 'an Shurb al-Dukhan' - I made it part of another treatise named 'Tarvih al-Jinan bi Tashrih Hukm Shurb al-Dukhan'. And 'al-Insaf fi Hukm al-I'tikaf', and 'al-Ifsah 'an Hukm Shahadat al-Mar'ah fi al-Irda'', and 'Tuhfat al-Talabah fi Mash al-Ruqabah', and its commentary called 'Tuhfat al-Kumalah', and 'Sibahat al-Fikr fi al-Jahr bi al-Dhikr', and 'Ihkam al-Qantarah fi Ahkam al-Basmalah', and 'Ghayat al-Maqal fima Yata'allaq bi al-Ni'al', and its commentary called 'Zafr al-Anfal'. 'al-Hashashah bi Naqd al-Wudu' bi al-Qahqahah', and 'Khayr al-Khabar bi Adhan Khayr al-Bashar', and 'Raf' al-Sitr 'an Kayfiyyat Idkhal al-Mayyit wa Tawjihihi fi al-Qabr', and 'Qut al-Mughtadin bi Fath al-Muqtadin', and 'Ifadat al-Khayr fi al-Istiyak bi Siwak al-Ghayr', and 'al-Tahqiq al-'Ajib fi al-Tathwib', and 'al-Kalam al-Jalil fima Yata'allaq bi al-Mindil'. And 'Tuhfat al-Akhyar fi Ihya' Sunnah Sayyid al-Abrar', and its commentary called 'Nukhbat al-Anzar', and 'Iqamat al-Hujjah 'ala anna al-Ikthar fi al-Ta'abbud laysa bi Bid'ah', and 'Tuhfat al-Nubala' fima Yata'allaq bi Jama'at al-Nisa'', and 'Zajr al-Nas 'ala Inkar Athar Ibn 'Abbas', and 'al-Falak al-Dawwar fima Yata'allaq bi Ru'yah al-Hilal bi al-Nahar', and 'al-Falak al-Mashhun fi al-Ajwibah al-Kamilah li al-As'ilah al-'Ashrat al-Kamilah', and 'Intifa' al-Rahin wa al-Murtahin bi al-Marhun', and 'Zafr al-Amani bi Sharh al-Mukhtasar al-Mansub ila al-Jurjani' not yet completed, and 'Imam al-Kalam fima Yata'allaq bi al-Qira'ah Khalf al-Imam', and its commentary called 'Ta'liq al-Fawa'id al-'Izam'. And 'Tadwir al-Falak fi Husul al-Jama'ah bi al-Jinn wa al-Malak', and 'Nuzhat al-Fikr fi Subhat al-Dhikr' and its commentary called 'al-Nafhah', and 'al-Qawl al-Jazim fi Suqut al-Hadd bi Nikah al-Mahrim', and 'Akam al-Nafa'is fi Ada' al-Adhkar bi Lisan al-Faris', and 'Tuhfat al-Thiqat fi Tafadul al-Lughat', not completed up to these times. And 'Rad' al-Ikhwan 'amma Ahdathuhu fi Akhir Jum'ah Ramadan', and 'Risalah fi al-Ghaybah' not completed, and 'Risalah fi al-Ahadith al-Mawdu'ah' not completed, and 'Tabsirat al-Basa'ir fi Ma'rifat al-Awakhir' not completed, and 'Jam' al-Mawa'iz al-Hasanah li Khutab Shuhur al-Sunnah', 'al-Bayyinat 'ala Wujud al-Anbiya' fi al-Tabaqat'. And 'Dafi' al-Waswas fi Athar Ibn 'Abbas li-Allah', and 'al-Kalam al-Mubram fi Naqd al-Qawl al-Muhkam', and 'al-Kalam al-Mabrun fi Radd al-Qawl al-Mansur', and 'al-Sa'y al-Mashkur fi Radd al-Madhhab al-Ma'thur', 'Hidayat al-Mughtadhin fi Fath al-Muqtadin', and other than that. And I thank Allah continuously for granting my writings high acceptance, and making them praised by the tongues of students and the perfect ones, and granting them complete prevalence and general fame, until the distinguished ones from far lands and distant regions turned to them. (1) I have spoken in detail about the works of Imam al-Lakhnawi, the correctness of their attribution to him, and the verification of their names and numbers in a book I devoted to his biography and called 'al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi li al-Imam al-Lakhnawi', so there is sufficiency for anyone seeking more, and no need for repetition here. (2) Up to our present day, we still observe the amazing acceptance of the works of Imam al-Lakhnawi and satisfaction with his investigations.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section in which the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a super-commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, lists his own scholarly works. He begins with works in the science of biographies (tarajim) and history, mentioning several titles such as 'Husrat al-'Alam bi Wafat Marji' al-'Alam' and 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyyah'. He then notes introductions he wrote, including one for this very book. Following that, he lists works in fiqh, siyar, and hadith, including his earlier hashiah on Sharh al-Wiqayah called 'al-Hashiyah al-Qadimah', an unfinished commentary 'al-Si'ayah', and the present third hashiah 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah'. He also mentions many other works on diverse topics like the Muwatta' of Imam Muhammad, rulings on shaving the head, prayer, fasting, and social issues. The passage ends with a prayer of thanks and two editorial footnotes confirming the wide acceptance of the author's works. The author is identified as Imam al-Lakhnawi, a prominent Hanafi scholar. This list demonstrates his extensive scholarly output and the recognition it received.

Key Terms
التراجم (al-tarajim): The science of biographical evaluation of narrators and scholars; here used for works dedicated to biographies.
الحاشية (al-hāshiyah): A super-commentary or marginal annotation on a main text; here referring to the author's own hashiyas on Sharh al-Wiqayah, especially the third one called 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah.
شرح الوقاية (Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah): The commentary on 'Wiqayah al-Riwayah', a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author's hashiya is upon this sharh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Lakhnawi's extensive list of works demonstrates his mastery of fiqh, tarajim, and hadith, and underscores the value of comprehensive scholarship in the Hanafi tradition.
