Biography of Abu Ali al-Duqqaq
Biographical entry from a sharh work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the chain of transmission from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani to later Hanafi scholars using biographical entries.

Core Idea
Biographical entries preserve the isnad of the madhhab.

This passage introduces Abu Ali al-Duqqaq, a Hanafi scholar who authored a work on menstruation and taught Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i. Understanding such biographical details helps us appreciate the chain of transmission that preserved the Hanafi school's teachings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Locate the name and any kuniya or nisba. Here, Abu Ali al-Duqqaq (al-Duqqaq likely an occupational nisba).
2
Identify his teachers
The text states he was a student (talimidh) of Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi, who is from the companions of Imam Muhammad.
Chain: Imam Muhammad → Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi → Abu Ali al-Duqqaq
3
Identify his students
He taught Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i (Ahmad ibn al-Husayn).
4
Note his works and death year
He authored 'Kitab al-Hayd' and died in 317 AH. This helps date his transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۲. أبو علي الدقاق : له ذكر في باب العدة» من «كتاب النكاح»، هو مؤلف «كتاب الحيض»، أستاذ أبي سعيد البردعي)، أحمد بن الحسين، المتوفى سنة سبع عشرة وثلاثمئة، كذا ذكره التقى الفاسي" في كتابه «العقد الثمين في تاريخ البلد الأمين»، وهو تلميد موسى ! موسى بن نصر الرازي له، من أصحاب الإمام محمد (۳). كذا قال الكفوي ، وغيره (٤)
12. Abu Ali al-Duqqaq: He is mentioned in the chapter on ‘idda from the Book of Marriage. He is the author of 'Kitab al-Hayd', teacher of Abu Sa‘id al-Barda‘i, Ahmad ibn al-Husayn, died in the year 317 AH. Thus mentioned by al-Taqi al-Fasi in his book 'al-‘Iqd al-Thamin fi Tarikh al-Balad al-Amin'. He was a student of Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi, from the companions of Imam Muhammad (3). So al-Kafawi and others said (4).
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This entry introduces Abu Ali al-Duqqaq, a Hanafi scholar who authored a work on menstruation (Kitab al-Hayd). He taught Abu Sa‘id al-Barda‘i, and studied under Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi, a disciple of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. His death year is 317 AH. The sources include al-‘Iqd al-Thamin by al-Fasi and Tabaqat works.

Key Terms
أصحاب الإمام محمد (aṣḥāb al-Imām Muḥammad): Students and direct transmitters from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Al-Taqi al-Fasi
C) Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi
D) Ahmad ibn al-Husayn

Key Takeaway
Abu Ali al-Duqqaq is a Hanafi scholar whose biography links the early transmission from Imam Muhammad's companions to later scholars.

Biography of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi: A Hanafi Jurist and Theologian
Biographical entry on Abu Mansur al-Maturidi from the sharh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and explain his significance to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Abu Mansur al-Maturidi linked Hanafi fiqh to Sunni theology through his works and scholarly chain.

This biographical entry introduces Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (d. 333 AH), a pivotal Hanafi scholar who combined jurisprudence with systematic theology. Though often remembered for his theological works, his direct chain to Abu Hanifa through two generations of Hanafi jurists confirms his authority in fiqh as well. Let us examine the details of his life, his writings, and his place in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisba
Notice the detailed spelling of 'Maturid' – a village near Samarkand. The nisba indicates his origin.
Al-Maturidi's full name: Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi.
2
Note the places where he appears in 'Umdat al-Ri'aya
The commentator mentions that al-Maturidi is referenced in the chapters on zakat and agency. This shows his works were used as sources in Hanafi fiqh texts.
3
List his major works
The entry lists 'Kitab al-Tawhid', 'Kitab al-Maqalat', 'Radd Dala’il al-Ka‘bi' (a refutation of a Mu‘tazili), and 'Ta’wilat al-Qur’an'. These show his theological and exegetical contributions.
The work 'Ta’wilat al-Qur’an' is a major tafsir.
4
Trace the academic chain to Abu Hanifa
The chain: Abu Mansur al-Maturidi studied under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, who studied under Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, who studied under Muhammad (al-Shaybani), who studied under Abu Hanifa. This establishes his direct link to the founder of the school.
This chain is recorded in 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya' by al-Kafawi and al-Qari.
5
Record the date of death
He died in 333 AH. This places him in the later period of the early Hanafi tradition, after the formative century.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۳. أبو منصور الماتريدي : له ذكر في باب زكاة السوائم» من «كتاب الزكاة»، وفي «باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء من كتاب الوكالة»، هو محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي، نسبة إلى ماتريد : بالميم بعدها ألف، ثم تاء مثناة فوقية مضمومة، ثم راء مهملة مكسورة، ثم ياء مثناة تحتية ساكنة ، قرية من قرى سمرقند، ذكره السَّمْعَانِي. ويقال له : إمام الهدى له : «كتاب التوحيد»، و«كتاب المقالات»، و«كتاب ردّ دلائل الكعبي وهو من معتزلة بغداد و كتاب تأويلات القرآن»، وغير ذلك، مات سنة ثلاث وثلاثين وثلاثمئة ، وتلمذ هو على أبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني، عن أبي سليمان الجوزجاني، عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة . كذا في «طبقات الحنفية» للكفوي (7)~ والقاري (1).
13. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi: He is mentioned in the chapter on zakat of grazing livestock from the Book of Zakat, and in the chapter on agency for sale and purchase from the Book of Agency. He is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi, relative to Maturid: with a meem followed by alif, then ta marbuta with damma, then ra with kasra, then ya sakinah, a village near Samarkand. Al-Sam‘ani mentioned him. He is called Imam al-Huda. He authored 'Kitab al-Tawhid', 'Kitab al-Maqalat', 'Kitab Radd Dala'il al-Ka‘bi' (al-Ka‘bi being from the Mu‘tazila of Baghdad), 'Ta'wilat al-Qur'an', and others. He died in the year 333 AH. He studied under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, who studied under Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, who studied under Muhammad, who studied under Abu Hanifa. So it is in 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya' by al-Kafawi and al-Qari.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This entry covers Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, a key figure in both Hanafi fiqh and theology (kalam). It lists his full name, nisba, and works. Notably, he wrote against the Mu‘tazili al-Ka‘bi. His death in 333 AH is given. The spiritual chain is traced through Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, and Muhammad al-Shaybani back to Abu Hanifa, emphasizing his authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
إمام الهدى (Imām al-Hudā): Title meaning 'Leader of Guidance', applied to al-Maturidi.
معتزلة (Mu‘tazila): An early Islamic theological school emphasizing reason and justice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To which village is al-Maturidi's nisba attributed?
A) Samarkand
B) Maturid, a village near Samarkand
C) Bukhara
D) Nishapur

Key Takeaway
Abu Mansur al-Maturidi was a Hanafi jurist and theologian who wrote influential works and whose chain to Abu Hanifa affirms his authority in the school.

Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: A Prolific Hanafi Authority
Biographical entry listing a Hanafi scholar and his works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi's key biographical details and list his major works, explaining their significance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi shaped Hanafi fiqh through his manuals and nawazil collections.

This passage introduces us to one of the great Hanafi scholars of Central Asia: Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, known as Imam al-Huda. He studied under Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani and authored numerous works that became essential references in the school. Understanding his contributions helps us appreciate the transmission and development of Hanafi legal knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his title
Focus on the name 'Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi' and his honorific 'Imam al-Huda' (Guide of the Community). Note that his full name is Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad.
The Arabic text has a slight corruption ('أبو الليث الله') but the correct is 'أبو الليث'.
2
Identify his teacher
He is a student of Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani. Knowing the teacher-scholar chain (isnad) is important for understanding the transmission of fiqh.
Al-Hindawani was a major Hanafi authority in Transoxiana.
3
List his major works
The passage lists several works: Tanbih al-Ghafilin (spiritual exhortation), al-Bustan (possibly similar), Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir (commentary on a core Hanafi text), al-Nawazil, al-'Uyun, al-Fatawa, Khizanat al-Fiqh, an introduction to fiqh, and a tafsir.
These works cover tafsir, hadith, fiqh, and fatwa collections.
4
Categorize the works by genre
Group them: fiqh manuals (Khizanat al-Fiqh, introduction), commentaries (Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir), fatwa collections (al-Nawazil, al-'Uyun, al-Fatawa), and other genres (Tanbih, Tafsir).
This shows his breadth as a scholar.
5
Assess his significance
Reflect on why these works are important: Khizanat al-Fiqh became a standard reference, and his nawazil works compiled actual fatwas for later jurists.
He is often cited in later Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۴. أبو الليث الله : له ذكر في باب المهر» من «كتاب النكاح»، هو الفقيه نصر بن محمد بن أحمد السَّمَرْقَنْدِي، المعروف بإمام الهدى، تلميذ الفقيه أبي جعفر الهندواني، لــه : «تنبيه الغافلين»، و«البستان»، و«شرح الجامع الصغير»، و«النوازل» و«العيون»، و«الفتاوي»، و«خزانة الفقه»، والمقدمة المشهورة في الفقه، وتفسير القرآن.
14. Abu al-Layth Alla: He is mentioned in the chapter on mahr from the Book of Marriage. He is the jurist Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, known as Imam al-Huda, student of the jurist Abu Ja‘far al-Hindawani. He authored: 'Tanbih al-Ghafilin', 'al-Bustan', 'Sharh al-Jami‘ al-Saghir', 'al-Nawazil', 'al-‘Uyun', 'al-Fatawa', 'Khizanat al-Fiqh', the famous introduction to fiqh, and a tafsir of the Quran.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This entry is on Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, a prolific Hanafi author. His full name is Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, titled Imam al-Huda. He was a student of Abu Ja‘far al-Hindawani. The passage lists many well-known works, including popular books like 'Tanbih al-Ghafilin' (a moral work), 'al-Bustan', a commentary on al-Jami‘ al-Saghir, collections of legal cases (Nawazil, ‘Uyun, Fatawa), a fiqh manual (Khizanat al-Fiqh), an introduction to fiqh, and a tafsir. His fame rests on these widely circulated works.

Key Terms
النوازل (al-nawāzil): Legal cases that occur, often unprecedented, requiring fatwa.
خزانة الفقه (Khizānat al-fiqh): 'Treasure of Fiqh', a manual of Hanafi law by Abu al-Layth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a work of Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi?
A) Tanbih al-Ghafilin
B) Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) Al-Mabsut
D) Tafsir al-Qur'an

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi was a prolific Hanafi jurist whose works—especially Khizanat al-Fiqh and al-Nawazil—became key references for later scholars.
